  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_47805bdb-50dd-4be1-b4f8-74bdd6bb78a6'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer14938631647137713751"><strong>Gossip Girl meets the Gilded Age in this delicious and compelling novel, the third in the <em>New York Times </em>bestselling series from author Anna Godbersen.</strong><br/><br/>In the thrilling third installment of Anna Godbersen’s bestselling Luxe series, Manhattan’s most envied residents appear to have everything they desire: Wealth. Beauty. Happiness. But sometimes the most practiced smiles hide</span>
  <span id="freeText14938631647137713751" style="display:none"><strong>Gossip Girl meets the Gilded Age in this delicious and compelling novel, the third in the <em>New York Times </em>bestselling series from author Anna Godbersen.</strong><br /><br />In the thrilling third installment of Anna Godbersen’s bestselling Luxe series, Manhattan’s most envied residents appear to have everything they desire: Wealth. Beauty. Happiness. But sometimes the most practiced smiles hide the most scandalous secrets.<br /><br /><em>
  <strong>Jealous whispers. Old rivalries. New betrayals. This is Manhattan, 1899.</strong>
</em><br /><br />Two months after Elizabeth Holland’s dramatic homecoming, Manhattan eagerly awaits her return to the pinnacle of society. When Elizabeth refuses to rejoin her sister Diana’s side, however, those watching New York’s favorite family begin to suspect that all is not as it seems behind the stately doors of No. 17 Gramercy Park South.<br /><br />Farther uptown, Henry and Penelope Schoonmaker are the city’s most celebrated couple. But despite the glittering diamond ring on Penelope’s finger, the newlyweds share little more than scorn for each other. And while the newspapers call Penelope’s social-climbing best friend, Carolina Broad, an heiress, her fortune—and her fame—is anything but secure.<br /><br /><strong>“Mystery, romance, jealousy, betrayal, humor, and gorgeous, historically accurate details. I couldn’t put <em>The Luxe </em>down!” —Cecily von Ziegesar, author of the #1 <em>New York Times </em>bestselling Gossip Girl series</strong></span>

      </div>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1355964-ok-just-short-little-question-but-in-the">Ok just short little question but in the prologue it enters by talking about the end and I&#39;ve figured out everyone else but who was the first person it talked about? Then Lena and Elizabeth and Diana and I think Penelope too but who was the first?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1355964'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F3347892-envy">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1355964-ok-just-short-little-question-but-in-the">See all 2 answers</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/6496061-elia"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1528337554i/6496061._UX100_CR0,16,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/6496061-elia">Elia</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The first person is Penelope's mother in law, and the man is Penelope's brother Grayson (it refers to her as a "matron" so that is someone older and m<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The first person is Penelope's mother in law, and the man is Penelope's brother Grayson (it refers to her as a "matron" so that is someone older and married, plus Penelope is mentioned later). Elizabeth is second, then Lena, then Henry and Penelope, with Diana last, being the only one whose name is given. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7309444941040611279"><i>"The paintings in this gallery are particularly nice."</i><br/><br/>I laughed when I came across this quote near the end of the novel because it very aptly sums up how painfully dull this series actually is. <i>And yet...</i> I continue to read. Somehow Anna Godbersen manages to capture my attention with every new chapter. And somehow my loyalties jump from character to character no matter how selfish or stupid they act. One minute I'm rooting for Diana, the next I'm scheming with Penelope, and finally I'm wondering</span>
  <span id="freeText7309444941040611279" style="display:none"><i>"The paintings in this gallery are particularly nice."</i><br /><br />I laughed when I came across this quote near the end of the novel because it very aptly sums up how painfully dull this series actually is. <i>And yet...</i> I continue to read. Somehow Anna Godbersen manages to capture my attention with every new chapter. And somehow my loyalties jump from character to character no matter how selfish or stupid they act. One minute I'm rooting for Diana, the next I'm scheming with Penelope, and finally I'm wondering why the two don't just become friends and push the abominable Henry Schoonmaker off a cliff.<br /><br />If you liked the first two books in the <i>Luxe</i> series, this one does not disappoint. And now I suppose I'll have to pick up <i>Splendor</i> and find out how this vapid story ends...</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10826919024075320452">#1.) The Luxe ★★★<br/>#2.) Rumours ★★.5<br/>#3.) Envy ★★<br/><br/><b>why do I keep reading these books? Please send help. </b><br/><br/>With every instalment I read, my<b> enjoyment along with my sanity goes downhill.</b> I blame the perfectionist in me, because I need to finish the series! Even if I really don't care, I want to tick off another series from my TBR, and seeing one more book left to read<i> kills me a little inside. </i><br/><br/>Luckily my library has the audiobooks of these available, so I can mindlessly read them rather than <b>wasting brai</b></span>
  <span id="freeText10826919024075320452" style="display:none">#1.) The Luxe ★★★<br />#2.) Rumours ★★.5<br />#3.) Envy ★★<br /><br /><b>why do I keep reading these books? Please send help. </b><br /><br />With every instalment I read, my<b> enjoyment along with my sanity goes downhill.</b> I blame the perfectionist in me, because I need to finish the series! Even if I really don't care, I want to tick off another series from my TBR, and seeing one more book left to read<i> kills me a little inside. </i><br /><br />Luckily my library has the audiobooks of these available, so I can mindlessly read them rather than <b>wasting brain cells reading them physically. </b><br /><br />That being said, this series is (evidently) quite addictive in trashy, gossip filled way. It serves as escapism for me, and I mostly read them for the world. The 1900's New York setting is really well done for the most part and I can feel as if I have been transported to the time period. <br /><br />I am typically quite a character driven reader, but I despise most of these characters. I feel as though Lina in particular has retrogressed, and become selfish, spoiled and self absorbed. I hope the last book talks about how her behaviour is wrong, but to be honest I don't have much hope for the finale. <br /><br /><b>Wish me luck!</b></span>

<div id="review_81205006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81205006" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2098381-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474068564p2/2098381.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81205006?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/2098381-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2098381-heather?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81205006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13342425387369853304">Oh the angst! My heart bleeds. Henry made me cry. Diana made me grit my teeth and Elizabeth made me sigh in exasperation. What's next I ask you?<br/><br/>While this series is ridiculous and completely over the top, it is a fabby guilty pleasure read. I swear the characters, apart from Penelope, are a few grapes short of a bushel, but vati are they entertaining.<br/><br/>Penelope has successfully trapped Henry into marring her, but because she is an evil, scheming wench, he is refusing to bed her, lol. She is certai</span>
  <span id="freeText13342425387369853304" style="display:none">Oh the angst! My heart bleeds. Henry made me cry. Diana made me grit my teeth and Elizabeth made me sigh in exasperation. What's next I ask you?<br /><br />While this series is ridiculous and completely over the top, it is a fabby guilty pleasure read. I swear the characters, apart from Penelope, are a few grapes short of a bushel, but vati are they entertaining.<br /><br />Penelope has successfully trapped Henry into marring her, but because she is an evil, scheming wench, he is refusing to bed her, lol. She is certain that if she can destroy Diana's reputation, she can win Henry back, as if she ever had him, and therefore assigning her brother, Grayson, the mission of re-deflowering Diana Holland. (For those of you new to this series, Henry had his way with Diana on a bear skinned rug in Rumors, vair entertaining). Alas, things don't quite work out as Penelope intended, surprise surprise.<br /><br />Elizabeth is still reeling from Will's death but is finding solace in Teddy Cutting, who just gets cuter by the minute. Sadly, Teddy, completely unaware of his appeal, sets out to war to win the respect and love of Elizabeth, which he was already well on his way of winning. This wouldn't be so bad if Elizabeth wasn't pregnant with Will's child. But she is and therefore ends up marrying Mr. Carnes in Teddy's absence. This caused me a great deal of frustration as I just know that Mr. Carnes is suspect and surely played a part in Will's unfortunate demise. Boo to that. Hopefully Mr. Carnes will meet a bad end and kick the bucket allowing Elizabeth to marry Teddy.<br /><br />Lina is in lurve with a new character, Leland, and though I can't stand her, I find myself wanting her to nab him. Odd. Even more to my chagrin was that I actually felt sorry for her when her patron died and secretly hoped that he would will her his fortune, which he did. Didn't see that one coming :)<br /><br />Diana. This character is frustrating to no end as she is quick to jump to conclusions, though I can't blame her, and causes her own troubles by following that hot temper of hers. But I like her, cause I would be a liar if I said that I didn't do the same things myself. I was a bit repulsed that she did the deed with Grayson, as he is described as having eyes that are too close together, and as a result, I was envisioning a #10 session with someone who looked like a fish. Hopefully she can find Henry in book 4 and put that disturbing image to rest.<br /><br />Henry, oh I still love Henry, though he is incredibly stupid. I was so annoyed with him throughout this book and was nearly ready to throw my copy across the room, but I just couldn't do it, cause I lobes him in spite of his stupidity. Just when I was about to loose all faith in him, he enlists and sends Diana a fabby letter that reduced me to tears, and once again, Henry has earned his way back into my good graces.<br /><br />Now all I have to decide is whether or not to run out to the store and buy Splendor in hardback or wait a year for it to come out in trade paper. Decisions decisions.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13342425387369853304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_46117620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46117620" />
    <a title="Angie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50378-angie"><img alt="Angie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510342996p2/50378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46117620?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie" href="/user/show/50378-angie">Angie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=bibliocrack">bibliocrack</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=good-uns">good-uns</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46117620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15673744905020591024">Third Luxe book and my favorite cover to date. Could just be that it's Diana on the cover and she's my favorite character...but I really like the dress. Actually, this is my favorite book of the three as well. And I really wasn't sure it would be. What with Henry and Penelope being...shudder. But this one seemed the most real. People grew up and, in a couple of notable cases, grew spines. Whether or not it will all be too little too late remains to be seen. The fourth (and final) Luxe book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7733.Gulliver_s_Travels__Penguin_Classics_' title='Gulliver's Travels (Penguin Classics) by Jonathan Swift' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sple</a></span>
  <span id="freeText15673744905020591024" style="display:none">Third Luxe book and my favorite cover to date. Could just be that it's Diana on the cover and she's my favorite character...but I really like the dress. Actually, this is my favorite book of the three as well. And I really wasn't sure it would be. What with Henry and Penelope being...shudder. But this one seemed the most real. People grew up and, in a couple of notable cases, grew spines. Whether or not it will all be too little too late remains to be seen. The fourth (and final) Luxe book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7733.Gulliver_s_Travels__Penguin_Classics_" title="Gulliver's Travels (Penguin Classics) by Jonathan Swift" rel="nofollow noopener">Splendor</a>, is due out in October and will hopefully settle a few things satisfactorily.<br /><br /><i>Envy</i> begins just a couple of months after the disastrous conclusion to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/571508.Rumors_of_War__Children_of_the_Promise__Vol_1_" title="Rumors of War (Children of the Promise, Vol 1) by Dean Hughes" rel="nofollow noopener">Rumors</a>. Elizabeth is inexplicably back on the scene, but not really <i>there</i>. Diana is floating through a fog of numb and trying to rise above the crushing blows that keep coming her way. Ditto for Henry. Lina is capitalizing on all her success and makes a surprisingly apt romantic choice. And Penelope is Penelope. You just want someone to stash her in a broom closet for Two Seconds so everyone else can take a deep breath and perhaps hatch a plan to put her in her place once and for all. And amid all this, everyone manages to sweep off on a trip to Palm Beach where much of the book takes place. <br /><br />I liked the change of scenery in this one. Putting everyone together in a Florida beach hotel for several days on end forced them all to interact despite the myriad tensions criss crossing between them. It also provided several quiet moments in which several characters reflected on how they ended up in the nasty mess they're in. It was nice to see some talk of doing the right thing at the cost of short-term (even long-term) happiness. Though I do hope happiness is in the cards for the most deserving (read: Teddy, Elizabeth, Diana, Henry). I liked this one best because it seemed the most natural. Every single character, at one point or another, was able to see beyond themselves for a moment to the people around them. I hope they remember what the view was like. This continues to be a diverting series and I look forward to its conclusion. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15673744905020591024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chloe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chloe" href="/user/show/1871569-chloe">Chloe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer42059867&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer42059867" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6384568292289236425">Just like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6185.Wuthering_Heights' title='Wuthering Heights by Emily Brontë' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Luxe</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/571508.Rumors_of_War__Children_of_the_Promise__Vol_1_' title='Rumors of War (Children of the Promise, Vol 1) by Dean Hughes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rumors</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/80536.Little_Earthquakes' title='Little Earthquakes by Jennifer Weiner' rel='nofollow noopener'>Envy</a> was completely addicting. I got it one morning and finished it before noon the next day. This one was more mature than the others in a way, since the characters have grown and experienced so much. I think my favorite girl in the series has become Diana: I can relate to her the most and I think that she is the most "real" and that she faces the hardest challenges. Elizabeth has become somewhat subdued and predictable.. I immediately suspected her pregnancy, alt</span>
  <span id="freeText6384568292289236425" style="display:none">Just like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6185.Wuthering_Heights" title="Wuthering Heights by Emily Brontë" rel="nofollow noopener">The Luxe</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/571508.Rumors_of_War__Children_of_the_Promise__Vol_1_" title="Rumors of War (Children of the Promise, Vol 1) by Dean Hughes" rel="nofollow noopener">Rumors</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/80536.Little_Earthquakes" title="Little Earthquakes by Jennifer Weiner" rel="nofollow noopener">Envy</a> was completely addicting. I got it one morning and finished it before noon the next day. This one was more mature than the others in a way, since the characters have grown and experienced so much. I think my favorite girl in the series has become Diana: I can relate to her the most and I think that she is the most "real" and that she faces the hardest challenges. Elizabeth has become somewhat subdued and predictable.. I immediately suspected her pregnancy, although her marriage to Snowden Cairns WAS a surprise. Penelope continues to make me angry with her manipulation and shallow-ness. Lina is also rather frustrating as she goes between appearing to accept her true beginnings and continuing to live the lie of richness. The prologue was confusing at first, but it made more sense at the end of the book since it was a flash-forward. I LOVED the ending and I cannot wait for <u>Splendor</u> to come out. This book was extremely well-written, interesting, and romantic. Great job Anna Godbersen! </span>
  <a data-text-id="6384568292289236425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_45094786" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45094786" />
    <a title="Amber" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1808070-amber"><img alt="Amber" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231809709p2/1808070.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45094786?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber" href="/user/show/1808070-amber">Amber</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1808070-amber?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer45094786&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45094786" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14906941516176489338">Ok, so while I still love this series, I didn't love this one as much as the ones before. In the beginning of the book, I found drunk Henry to be amusing, but it just kept going and he was being so harsh to Penelope. Yes, I know it's her own fault, but I still felt bad for her. And, I just felt like the scenes with Henry and Diana back and forth were too much of the same, it bored me after awhile.<br/><br/>As for Elizabeth, I found her annoying through most of this book. She was supposed to be helping Di </span>
  <span id="freeText14906941516176489338" style="display:none">Ok, so while I still love this series, I didn't love this one as much as the ones before. In the beginning of the book, I found drunk Henry to be amusing, but it just kept going and he was being so harsh to Penelope. Yes, I know it's her own fault, but I still felt bad for her. And, I just felt like the scenes with Henry and Diana back and forth were too much of the same, it bored me after awhile.<br /><br />As for Elizabeth, I found her annoying through most of this book. She was supposed to be helping Di but was just a sleeping, frail little thing. I know we found out that she's knocked up, and granted I've never been pregnant, but I thought they went a little far with the weak and frail descriptions. I was happy for her when she grew closer to Teddy, and I'm really glad they did more with his character in this book. I was unhappy with how this book ended for Elizabeth's sake though, hasn't she been through enough. Couldn't she have married Teddy and then have him rush off to war? Why before? <br /><br />Onto Diana again. While I look forward to her pretending to be a boy in the next book and chasing down Henry(does anyone know when it comes out?), I found the whole thing to be a little far fetched. <br /><br />Well, at least, Carolina got a happy ending, not that I care much for her, but she's growing on me.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14906941516176489338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_139199857" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139199857" />
    <a title="Anne Osterlund" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2232237-anne-osterlund"><img alt="Anne Osterlund" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442481722p2/2232237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139199857?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne Osterlund" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne Osterlund" href="/user/show/2232237-anne-osterlund">Anne Osterlund</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139199857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12641011392530159166">Anna Godbersen’s Luxe series is an exercise in contradictions. Exquisite in its descriptions of the phenomenal wealth of turn of the century New York society. Outrageous in its catastrophic tumbling into the depraved values of said society. And drive-you-up-the-wall in its depictions of flawed selfish characters. For whom— for no discernible reason—you still wish things would go well.<br/><br/>Even though I hate Penelope (who I’m definitely supposed to hate). And I despise Carolina (who I still don’t want</span>
  <span id="freeText12641011392530159166" style="display:none">Anna Godbersen’s Luxe series is an exercise in contradictions. Exquisite in its descriptions of the phenomenal wealth of turn of the century New York society. Outrageous in its catastrophic tumbling into the depraved values of said society. And drive-you-up-the-wall in its depictions of flawed selfish characters. For whom— for no discernible reason—you still wish things would go well.<br /><br />Even though I hate Penelope (who I’m definitely supposed to hate). And I despise Carolina (who I still don’t want to see fall on her face). And I find Elizabeth mind-numbingly weak (What was she thinking coming back home?) And the best I can say for Diana and Henry is that they deserve each other.<br /><br />The fact is that I loved the final scene of Envy.<br /><br />And I will be back for more. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12641011392530159166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_35493157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35493157" />
    <a title="Sarah MacLean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/216457-sarah-maclean"><img alt="Sarah MacLean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499444202p2/216457.jpg" /></a>

  <span id="freeText17280971358002925187" style="display:none">This is the type of book you just can’t stop reading because you have to know the outcome. <div id="review_156828984" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156828984" />
    <a title="Meera K." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1621451-meera-k"><img alt="Meera K." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309562464p2/1621451.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156828984?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meera K." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meera K." href="/user/show/1621451-meera-k">Meera K.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156828984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6377560399243410801">OH GOD. I swear I've had a love hate relationship with these books. THEY'RE SO BAD THAT THEY'RE GOOD! Every minute I read Envy, all I was thinking about was some flaw with a stupid character in the book or the INCREDIBLY boring plot line. But I just HAD TO FIGURE OUT WHAT WOULD HAPPEN! And after I finished Envy at like 2 AM.. I got up and picked up Splendor. Doesn't sound like I hate them.. but believe me.. I HAVE SO MANY COMPLAINTS.<br/><br/>FIRSTLY: Stupid Characters<br/>Elizabeth: Okay, I understand the tra</span>
  <span id="freeText6377560399243410801" style="display:none">OH GOD. I swear I've had a love hate relationship with these books. THEY'RE SO BAD THAT THEY'RE GOOD! Every minute I read Envy, all I was thinking about was some flaw with a stupid character in the book or the INCREDIBLY boring plot line. But I just HAD TO FIGURE OUT WHAT WOULD HAPPEN! And after I finished Envy at like 2 AM.. I got up and picked up Splendor. Doesn't sound like I hate them.. but believe me.. I HAVE SO MANY COMPLAINTS.<br /><br />FIRSTLY: Stupid Characters<br />Elizabeth: Okay, I understand the trauma because her husband was killed.. but why does Godbersen have to give her these sudden feelings for Teddy? Do all the characters have to be heartbroken? And then when Teddy leaves for war and Elizabeth "sinks into her chair with regret" or whatever, it made me want to puke. So, husband dead, you immediately have to go back for the second choice. But when Snowden decided to marry her.. I thought that was incredibly sweet. And really good that Elizabeth didn't complain that he wasn't handsome or whatever.<br /><br />Diana: Even though she's my favorite character.. EH. I guess that I can understand her desperate need for Henry, and visa versa. The whole Grayson thing was a little unnecessary and weird. Plus, it seems like all the guys that run after her just follow her for her "rosy cheeks" and "dreamy lashes" and her youngness. Firstly, pedophile alert... and secondly, it totally makes their love seem fake. They say and think all the right things, but the "I can't live without you" crap seems to be a little put on.<br /><br />Penelope: I get that she's the bitch character... but I wish Godbersen try to make her seem a little more wanted. She's portrayed as this TOTAL bad guy.. which is WAY too unrealistic. She's supposed to be incredibly beautiful like the rest of them. THEN SHOW IT! Have someone come after her too! Have her seem nice. Put the Holland sisters in the bad position!! Diana continues to lust after Henry even though he's married. MAKE THAT SEEM LIKE A BAD THING! Don't make Penelope the ONLY BAD GUY! <br /><br />Lina: Only character that seems to get a happy ending, SHE moved on from loving Will.. but then again, she wasn't the one married to him. Only problem: but her life seems to be getting so distant from Elizabeth, Diana, and Penelope. Especially SPLENDOR ALERT! when Claire starts working for someone else, Lina has no inside into the Holland's anymore. She's not intertwined with their lives. I haven't finished Splendor... so I hope before I do, they turn that around.<br /><br />SECONDLY: Plot line<br />The overall story was so PREDICTABLE. And wayy to over the top with the thoughts from the heart broken lovers "I want to be with her so bad.. I felt like I was dying" or whatever. I felt like laughing. SO CHEESY.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6377560399243410801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_51983970" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51983970" />
    <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip"><img alt="Jennifer Wardrip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442657515p2/1125613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/51983970?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=read-by-other-reviewers">read-by-other-reviewers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51983970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10167363413081202852">Reviewed by Sarah Bean the Green Bean Teen Queen for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>It's 1900 in New York, and scandal and gossip are never far behind.<br/><br/>Elizabeth Holland is back and everyone is awaiting her re-entrance into society. But things are not as they seem in No. 17 Gramercy Park. Elizabeth and her sister, Diana, are both grieving the loss of their loved ones. When the sisters are invited along on a trip to Florida by the newly married Schoonmakers, they decide this is the perfect escape.<br/><br/>Penelope Schoon</span>
  <span id="freeText10167363413081202852" style="display:none">Reviewed by Sarah Bean the Green Bean Teen Queen for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />It's 1900 in New York, and scandal and gossip are never far behind.<br /><br />Elizabeth Holland is back and everyone is awaiting her re-entrance into society. But things are not as they seem in No. 17 Gramercy Park. Elizabeth and her sister, Diana, are both grieving the loss of their loved ones. When the sisters are invited along on a trip to Florida by the newly married Schoonmakers, they decide this is the perfect escape.<br /><br />Penelope Schoonmaker isn't pleased to invite the woman her husband is in love with along on her trip, but she knows she must keep her enemies close if she's ever going to get what she wants.<br /><br />Carolina Broad is climbing high in society, but her place is not secure and her newfound fame and fortune could disappear any moment.<br /><br />I've been addicted to the LUXE series since it began, and ENVY continues to add more gossip and scandal to the story. I thought the twists and turns in ENVY moved the story along quicker than the previous two stories. I loved that the author moved a lot of the action to Florida - it added new scenery and lots of fun situations. There were many times I told myself "just one more chapter" because I needed to know what would happen next.<br /><br />Each chapter tells a part of the story from a different character and I found myself enjoying each storyline this time around. Yes, I still wanted to yell at Penelope, would get annoyed at Carolina's social climbing, and tell Diana not to make so many assumptions, but I think that's part of the fun of the series.<br /><br />Anna Godbersen does such a great job at getting the readers involved in the characters that you can't help but cheer them on, or even root against them. I also thought there were some characters this time around who got stronger and started to stand up for themselves, so I'm eager to see where they end up.<br /><br />I will be first in line to get my hands on a copy of SPLENDOR, the next book in the LUXE series, when it's released.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10167363413081202852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33365986?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/104823-kate">Kate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104823-kate?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104823-kate?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104823-kate?shelf=age-ya">age-ya</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33365986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2626484668419012767">This third installment of the Luxe series was just as good as the first two books. The relationships between the characters are tangled and soap-opera dramatic, but nothing so confusing that I couldn't follow the story line from the first book. As with the first two books, the prologue hints at the ending, but by the time I got to the ending, what I had imagined to be happening was something entirely different - in a good way. <br/><br/>The one nit-picky thing that bugged me was how the author describes C</span>
  <span id="freeText2626484668419012767" style="display:none">This third installment of the Luxe series was just as good as the first two books. The relationships between the characters are tangled and soap-opera dramatic, but nothing so confusing that I couldn't follow the story line from the first book. As with the first two books, the prologue hints at the ending, but by the time I got to the ending, what I had imagined to be happening was something entirely different - in a good way. <br /><br />The one nit-picky thing that bugged me was how the author describes Carolina's lips as "bee-stung" on more than one occasion. Okay, I get it, the girl has big puffy voluptuous Angelina Jolie lips. That's at least three adjectives right there other than "bee-stung" to describe her lips (I have to deduct "Angelina Jolie" as an adjective as this is a historical fiction). I could go on with less flattering descriptors, such as "trout-like" or "inflated." But really, this was the only thing that bugged me. Other than all the girls having tiny little waists and tiny little bodies except for trout-faced, freckle-bespotted, and man-handed Carolina, but of course Carolina was born into the servant class, and obviously genetics cannot overcome the caste system and decades of inbreeding.<br /><br />I just hope that everyone ends up with who they should in the fourth and final Luxe novel, <i>Splendor</i>: Elizabeth and Teddy, Henry and Diana, Carolina and Leland, and Penelope with no one. Or maybe Penelope and her brother Grayson. Or possibly Tristan. Or some creepy old man.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2626484668419012767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5381051118347026495">Oh brother. I can't believe that I just wasted my precious time reading this whole book. The writing is laughable. In the last book, people were always feeling the anger/rage burning the back of their throats. This time, Diana looked so beautiful, Henry was feeling it in his knees.   <span id="freeText5381051118347026495" style="display:none">Oh brother. I can't believe that I just wasted my precious time reading this whole book. The writing is laughable. In the last book, people were always feeling the anger/rage burning the back of their throats. This time, Diana looked so beautiful, Henry was feeling it in his knees. And what's the deal with clavicles? They mentioned several times throughout this book- either someone is looking at their clavicles in the mirror, or a dress is showing them off. Weird.Sometimes I felt like she was writing with a thesaurus sitting next to her. It was the same thing over and over again, with certain new words substituted for other words, in exactly the same sentence. The plot was entirely predictable. I knew from the first minute it mentioned Elizabeth's tiredness what her "condition" would be. When Teddy decides that he is going to join the Army, it's easy to tell this will be Henry's way out, too. I don't like the story of the former maid Lina (Carolina) I find her character annoying, and at the end, I mostly barely skimmed anything relating to her. The only unexpected plot twist was Elizabeth's marriage. To me, Mr. Cairns was such a non-entity, I didn't even remember who he was when he first re-appeared to marry her. <br />The saddest part of all is that I will most likely read the next book in the series when it comes out. Since it is the last book, I might as well, since I have vested so much time in these characters. </span>

  <span id="freeText12181177795264488909" style="display:none">Tahle série mě pořád baví! Gossip girl je prostě moje. Penelopa jede. Upřímně mě jen štve Lina, jejíž PoV fakt nemám ráda. Ugh. Drama, drama, drama... can't wait for the last book. <br /><br />3.5/5*<br /><br /><b>English Review:</b><br /><br />Envy starts where Rumours ended. Our four heroines deal with problems concerning their popularity and social status. Gossip Girl set in 20th century comes with a new challenges, including a trip to Florida. I was quite happy with this plot twist because surroundings in NY get quite repetitive after two books. The story was satisfying enough, fast paced and gripping in times. <br /><br />The whole series mostly focuses on relationships and keeping social status in society. So, if you are not entertained by gossips and lot of drama, avoid this series. 5 PoVs, 4 girls and 1 boy. We can clearly see the character progress indeed, eventhough I didn't like all of it. Penelope is still my most favourite character, followed by Henry, probably. I like Elizabeth, eventhough she was rather sad and depressed in this book. I understand why but still... Diana is still annoying and naive. Really, when is it gonna stop? And Lina... my most hated character. I understand where she's coming from, but I hate the way she acts. <br /><br />Not only does this series have beautiful covers, it is also very entertaining. I enjoy this type of books from time to time, and summer is perfect opportunity for them. Can't wait for the final book. <br /><br />3.5/5*<br /></span>

<div id="review_121124673" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121124673" />
    <a title="YA Reads Book Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1764232-ya-reads-book-reviews"><img alt="YA Reads Book Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285429046p2/1764232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121124673?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YA Reads Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YA Reads Book Reviews" href="/user/show/1764232-ya-reads-book-reviews">YA Reads Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121124673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4613329847325231818">Envy is the third instalment in The Luxe series. It picks up right where Rumors left off, with enough scandal to drive even the calmest of readers’ crazy.<br/><br/>Mr Henry Schoonmaker – one of New York’s most eligible bachelors, and the love of Diana Holland’s life – has a new wife, and he’s not one bit happy about it, either. How could he be, when the love of his life is not the woman to whom he is now legally bound? Henry can’t even bring himself to look at Penelope with affection so how is he going to</span>
  <span id="freeText4613329847325231818" style="display:none">Envy is the third instalment in The Luxe series. It picks up right where Rumors left off, with enough scandal to drive even the calmest of readers’ crazy.<br /><br />Mr Henry Schoonmaker – one of New York’s most eligible bachelors, and the love of Diana Holland’s life – has a new wife, and he’s not one bit happy about it, either. How could he be, when the love of his life is not the woman to whom he is now legally bound? Henry can’t even bring himself to look at Penelope with affection so how is he going to fulfil his physical requirements as a husband? As Henry drinks himself stupid night after night, hoping that the alcohol will numb his senses and dull the pain, Penelope’s scheming ways continue evermore.<br /><br />Diana Holland – the real love of Henry’s life, and the reason he married Penelope in the first place – is hurting. Although Henry told her that he married Penelope to protect her, that Penelope had threatened to tarnish Diana’s wholesome reputation by telling all of New York that Henry had taken her virginity out of wedlock, seeing him with Penelope all the time is a painful matter indeed. Now that he is no longer in the market for a wife, Diana is doing everything she can to put her feelings for Henry behind her, but love is relentless and he haunts her everywhere she goes. Will she be able to stay away from him, especially when he is asking her not to?<br /><br />The new Penelope Schoonmaker is watching Henry and Diana with hawke-like eyes. She is no fool and she can see the way the pair of them still look at each other. It makes her sick to the stomach to think of her husband’s eyes searching for someone else in the crowd, but honestly, what did she expect? She bribed him into marrying her in the first place. Penelope knows all too well that the only way she will keep her man is by bribing and manipulating him further. But will Henry put up with it for much longer? If the love of your life was slipping through your fingers, what would you do to be with them?<br /><br />Elizabeth Holland finds herself in quite the predicament indeed. Mourning the loss of her husband, and former servant, Elizabeth finds herself attracting the attention of a one Mr Teddy Cutting – again. Elizabeth feels alone, in despair. Will she warm to Mr Cutting’s affections this time around? Only time will tell. Elizabeth is honest with Mr Cutting about her feelings for him – that the timing is all wrong and she’s still in mourning. But then something happens, something that will ruin the Holland’s forever if Elizabeth doesn’t find a way to fix it. Being with Mr Cutting suddenly seems like a magnificent idea…<br /><br />And Carolina Broad is up to her usual tricks. I hate Lina so much that I can’t even bring myself to write anything about her.<br /><br />Envy delivers the goods. After reading Rumors I wasn’t so sure that Anna Godbersen would be able to top her effort – but I was wrong. She writes brilliantly and reading her work is effortless. Henry’s character is developed further in this instalment and he steps of the pages of Envy like a radiant, shining light. I find myself wondering how much more of Anna Godbersen’s scandalous world I can take. I can’t wait for Splendour (the fourth novel) and I know I’ll re-read Envy obsessively until I get my hands on it.<br /><br />Praise for Anna Godbersen, who has successfully reignited the 1900’s and made it totally cool to be all proper and old school. I love everything about this series – absolutely everything! This would make one hell of a killer television show.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4613329847325231818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1677901139" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1677901139" />
    <a title="Daphne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37016646-daphne"><img alt="Daphne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592518336p2/37016646.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1677901139?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daphne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daphne" href="/user/show/37016646-daphne">Daphne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141323381" href="/book/show/6433216-envy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37016646-daphne?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37016646-daphne?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37016646-daphne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37016646-daphne?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37016646-daphne?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37016646-daphne?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37016646-daphne?shelf=from-library-2016">from-library-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37016646-daphne?shelf=pb">pb</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1677901139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2430831163907785299">After reading <i>Rumors</i>, I took a break from this series and I think it was the right thing to do. The books aren't hard to follow and they are all very similar, so I think I would have enjoyed <i>Envy</i> less if I had read it right after Rumors. <br/><br/>Still, I didn't enjoy <i>Envy</i> as much as I enjoyed the first book in this series. I think it might have peaked there, if I'm honest, but the other books are still mindlessly entertaining. They are quick, light reads with lots of drama to keep you turning the page. </span>
  <span id="freeText2430831163907785299" style="display:none">After reading <i>Rumors</i>, I took a break from this series and I think it was the right thing to do. The books aren't hard to follow and they are all very similar, so I think I would have enjoyed <i>Envy</i> less if I had read it right after Rumors. <br /><br />Still, I didn't enjoy <i>Envy</i> as much as I enjoyed the first book in this series. I think it might have peaked there, if I'm honest, but the other books are still mindlessly entertaining. They are quick, light reads with lots of drama to keep you turning the page. Even if they are a little predictable. <br /><br />I have two reasons why this book did not get a 4 star rating. One is that I felt like the author relied too much on miscommunication as a way to keep the story from resolving too quickly. Henry and Diana had so much drama that could have been avoided with one single line of dialogue, and I wish it had been set up better. I did like their part of the story best, but it bothered me. <br /><br />The other reason is that there are issues in this story that get resolved way too easily. The author spends a lot of time setting up both Elizabeth and Carolina to have a big problem, only to resolve it in the easiest way she possibly could. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Elizabeth is pregnant from her secret late husband and conveniently marries someone nice and willing that knows about it and is fine with keeping the secret. Carolina loses the benefactor that has been financing her new lifestyle to an illness, only to discover that he left almost everything to her in his will. The girls barely get time to worry about their issues before they are solved.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Of course, I'm sure these things will get explored more in the last book, but I still felt like they were sort of cheap. <br /><br />Still, this series is fun and I'll finish it because I want to see how all this drama ends. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2430831163907785299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3026879483" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3026879483" />
    <a title="Cari Clayton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22196415-cari-clayton"><img alt="Cari Clayton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373812795p2/22196415.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3026879483?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cari Clayton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cari Clayton" href="/user/show/22196415-cari-clayton">Cari Clayton</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3026879483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3038481692219725807">This book reminds me of reading the third book in the original V.C. Andrews series, difficult to get through. It was still good story lines, getting us forward following the different characters, but dragged, dragged, dragged. I hope the fourth and final installment will have me more motivated to read. I went days without opening the pages. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_100123175" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100123175" />
    <a title="Jenben8426" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1233628-jenben8426"><img alt="Jenben8426" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100123175?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenben8426" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenben8426" href="/user/show/1233628-jenben8426">Jenben8426</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233628-jenben8426?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100123175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12999143304682802359">This series is just so Soap Opera"ish" to me! You get a couple together and then some evil character who looks absolutely beautiful comes and tears them apart. No one can say what is obvious to say which drives me bonkers. Again the book had potential but because of all the stupid drama it was hard to find the good. I think the story could have been much better and more entertaining if it wasn't so cliche. I again would say that this book needs to be read if you are 18 or older hence the adult t</span>
  <span id="freeText12999143304682802359" style="display:none">This series is just so Soap Opera"ish" to me! You get a couple together and then some evil character who looks absolutely beautiful comes and tears them apart. No one can say what is obvious to say which drives me bonkers. Again the book had potential but because of all the stupid drama it was hard to find the good. I think the story could have been much better and more entertaining if it wasn't so cliche. I again would say that this book needs to be read if you are 18 or older hence the adult title even while it is considered young adult. <br /><br />In the 3rd book, it has been two months since tragedy hit Elizabeth Holland's happy life. She hasn't left her home and now people are starting to talk about what is wrong with her. The Holland's still need a successful marriage to pull themselves up from financial ruin. Diana is heartbroken over Henry's unexpected marriage to the conniving Penelope but is determined to move on. And the once maid Carolina Broad is moving her way up the social ladder and is being quite successful. I found myself the most interested in the somewhat historical parts of the novel--especially the fashion of the rich and elite in the 1900s. I was annoyed by the social rules though--honestly these characters need a little backbone! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12999143304682802359" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_88447273" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/88447273" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/88447273?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-may-2010">zzread-may-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer88447273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12317521447493692248">Anna Godbersen has a very nice writing style. It's formal, yet relaxing to read. Her third book in the Luxe series, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3347892.Envy__Luxe___3_' title='Envy (Luxe, #3) by Anna Godbersen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Envy</a>, continues the story of the Diana and Elizabeth Holland, Penelope Hayes, and Carolina Broad. The books take place in New York at the turn of the century and it gives us a glimpse of high society and the proper etiquette of the period.<br/><br/>The books are addicting. I enjoyed the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1254951.The_Luxe__Luxe___1_' title='The Luxe (Luxe, #1) by Anna Godbersen' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Luxe</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2218252.Rumors__Luxe___2_' title='Rumors (Luxe, #2) by Anna Godbersen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rumors</a> so much that I read them both in one day. You feel for the characters and how they wer</span>
  <span id="freeText12317521447493692248" style="display:none">Anna Godbersen has a very nice writing style. It's formal, yet relaxing to read. Her third book in the Luxe series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3347892.Envy__Luxe___3_" title="Envy (Luxe, #3) by Anna Godbersen" rel="nofollow noopener">Envy</a>, continues the story of the Diana and Elizabeth Holland, Penelope Hayes, and Carolina Broad. The books take place in New York at the turn of the century and it gives us a glimpse of high society and the proper etiquette of the period.<br /><br />The books are addicting. I enjoyed the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1254951.The_Luxe__Luxe___1_" title="The Luxe (Luxe, #1) by Anna Godbersen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Luxe</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2218252.Rumors__Luxe___2_" title="Rumors (Luxe, #2) by Anna Godbersen" rel="nofollow noopener">Rumors</a> so much that I read them both in one day. You feel for the characters and how they were limited by their positions in society. You see how quickly a character can fall from grace, simply by the death of a benefactor or an indiscretion, or a loss of fortune.<br /><br />I would recommend this book and the series to anyone who enjoys a romantic, early 1900's read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12317521447493692248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8AK9QZR8i5TvuhG5HvQDTqeVa4Modue5XT+6A1/oVFamU/Fhws/eTfMxq/hUBNWPch5TmFnJUDx083dXzI1/og==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dMAWpc54XkmM1S2+e59xlyc76VvUpYunB74fxHTva14ikVqFmMsLkJBel/8xb6dW8rDRQKUaPCIuctKQ54pAqg==')})
  }
